    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17498078600781913113">Brian Keenan went to Beirut in 1985 for a change of scene from his native Belfast. He became headline news when he was kidnapped by fundamentalist Shi'ite militiamen and held in the suburbs of Beirut for the next four and a half years. For much of that time he was shut off from all news and contact with anyone other than his jailers and, later, his fellow hostages, amongst</span>

<div id="review_1901731750" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901731750" />
    <a title="Ana " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5237420-ana"><img alt="Ana " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573472177p2/5237420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901731750?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana " href="/user/show/5237420-ana">Ana </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=about-murders">about-murders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=absolute">absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=brainy-psychological">brainy-psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=fallen-characters">fallen-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=law-abiding-citizen">law-abiding-citizen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=of-life-and-death">of-life-and-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5237420-ana?shelf=of-self">of-self</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901731750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4299789247274830578">It is a rare occasion that you get to read a book that manages to surprise you from beginning to end. I didn’t expect anything out of it, but I still discovered I had a number of expectations, because I discovered them whilst I was reading something that seemed to contradict what I subconsciously thought. <br/><br/>This book is written with grace. Yes, grace is the right word. I imagine Keenan with his back straight and a steady hand as he wrote it – though how he could have managed that beats me. To be i</span>
  <span id="freeText4299789247274830578" style="display:none">It is a rare occasion that you get to read a book that manages to surprise you from beginning to end. I didn’t expect anything out of it, but I still discovered I had a number of expectations, because I discovered them whilst I was reading something that seemed to contradict what I subconsciously thought. <br /><br />This book is written with grace. Yes, grace is the right word. I imagine Keenan with his back straight and a steady hand as he wrote it – though how he could have managed that beats me. To be in captivity for almost five years, beaten, humiliated, forgotten, and to still write in such a graceful, poised way.. It can only speak of the character of this Irishman. The character that kept him going, the strength and intelligence that saved him from becoming as hateful as his guards. <br /><br />This book is a pure descent into insanity. Keenan’s mind went mad – and then, as only very few minds can do, he coerced himself out of that madness and became sane again. How, again, how he did this is beyond my ability to understand, because I have never been imprisoned or tortured. I can only clinically understand it – like pointing to the x on the treasure map – but the road there is one that only Keenan could take for himself. <br /><br />This book contains some of the most beautiful writing I have ever seen in my life. Leaving the subject matter aside (though hard to do…), the words themselves fold and float together in a web that tightens and loosens with every chapter, simulating the undulations of the human mind while suppressed and subjected to the most horrific terrors and the most painful tortures. It is, and I say this with my years of experience as a reader, a unique book through and through. I must confess that I strongly believe that this experience of Keenan’s, when for five years he only had the words and the images that his mind could create, completely shaped his writing. It is so intimate, so distressingly beautiful, that I found myself feeling guilty for reading and re-reading passages of his tortures or his insanity moments, because of how accurately and disturbingly he managed to express them on paper. <br /><br />This book is priceless to understanding the mentality of terrorists. Keenan describes their behavior and beliefs, their points of view. This is not just a book about being captive: this is a psychological study into understanding your captors. Absolutely, hauntingly beautiful, filled with lessons in moral strength and integrity that all of us should learn, but few of us ever get the chance to discover about themselves. <br /><br />This book has, in one swipe, climbed to the top of my favorite books ever. It crosses the borders of genres, styles and literary might because of its truth and the beauty of the mind of its writer. Truly astonishing, I have no more words of praise for it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4299789247274830578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_226643675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226643675" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5041353-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601285820p2/5041353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226643675?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/5041353-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5041353-jim?shelf=ireland-irish">ireland-irish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5041353-jim?shelf=inspirational-teaching">inspirational-teaching</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226643675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16150328170501295628">A much better book than might have been expected. Brian Keenan's nightmare incarceration of over 4 years at the hands of some Hezbollah fundamentalist thugs in Beirut has given rise to a remarkable work of literature. Keenan shows little interest in the politics of his captors, but considerable insight into their minds. They are young, religious and sexually repressed. They are more brutalised and diminished by the situation than the men they guard, and periodically beat. This book is at times a</span>
  <span id="freeText16150328170501295628" style="display:none">A much better book than might have been expected. Brian Keenan's nightmare incarceration of over 4 years at the hands of some Hezbollah fundamentalist thugs in Beirut has given rise to a remarkable work of literature. Keenan shows little interest in the politics of his captors, but considerable insight into their minds. They are young, religious and sexually repressed. They are more brutalised and diminished by the situation than the men they guard, and periodically beat. This book is at times almost unbearable to read, it brilliantly relates the static conditions of his captivity and the awful odyssey of his mind, how even the entry of an orange into their monotone world is a remarkable object of colour and beauty. It manages a near- perfect balance of narrative and reflection. It also portrays the strange friendship which develops between the Irish socialist(Keenan) and the English public schoolboy, John McCarthy and how they use their humour and friendship to survive such incarceration.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16150328170501295628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer279416827" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10034029594463888099">I first read this book shortly after it was published; it is an unforgettable account of brutality and the loss of freedom but also an uplifting account of hope, resilience and friendship. Brian was kidnapped and incarcerated in Beirut and over more than 4 years moved to various hiding places. The account of how he and fellow prisoner, John McCarthy were transported from place to place was both fascinating and horrible. I found myself holding my breath through the ordeal with them. Brian and Joh</span>
  <span id="freeText10034029594463888099" style="display:none">I first read this book shortly after it was published; it is an unforgettable account of brutality and the loss of freedom but also an uplifting account of hope, resilience and friendship. Brian was kidnapped and incarcerated in Beirut and over more than 4 years moved to various hiding places. The account of how he and fellow prisoner, John McCarthy were transported from place to place was both fascinating and horrible. I found myself holding my breath through the ordeal with them. Brian and John became staunch friends during the time they were together, at times mystifying other hostages who crossed their paths over the years, with their irreverant treatment of each other. <br />In contrast are the passages about illness and beatings were the men cared for each other and kept one another going. Brian Keegan writes with a beautiful and poetic honesty.<br />This book is an inspiration; I so admired Brian for his determination and humanity throughout and I still do. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10034029594463888099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676328242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17479977956060465860">Brian Keenan went to Beirut in 1985 for a change from his native Belfast. He was kidnapped and held for the next four and half years. It was here that he met fellow hostage John McCarthy. This is an amazing read; Brain is a man full of integrity and compassion and a quality writer. I could quote so many passages from this book but one stands out "I wanted to affirm that I was myself and would not allow my integrity to be taken from me by a surrender to what another believed or would make me be".</span>
  <span id="freeText17479977956060465860" style="display:none">Brian Keenan went to Beirut in 1985 for a change from his native Belfast. He was kidnapped and held for the next four and half years. It was here that he met fellow hostage John McCarthy. This is an amazing read; Brain is a man full of integrity and compassion and a quality writer. I could quote so many passages from this book but one stands out "I wanted to affirm that I was myself and would not allow my integrity to be taken from me by a surrender to what another believed or would make me be". Throughout the isolation, degrading treatement and abuse, Brian never lost his compassion for others "We cannot know ourselves or declare ourselves human unless we share in the humanity of another". </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3270723705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3947661115739075891">Within loneliness lies a unique world where each should find their own path to understand it. The author dredging up his life, while being a political prisoner, carves out this world into a reality in this book. The effect it brings out reaches out to all as a self reflection of oneself. The struggle and companionship along with the solitude he had had while he was a prisoner throws into light the mysterious ways mind can find its perseverance to remain sane while being lonely.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9974919219543928224">This wasn't a very easy read. <br/><br/>I'll start by saying that I started reading this book after I saw a Facebook comment claiming this is good literature. I was intrigued as Middle East history and people overcoming struggles are things I enjoy reading about. <br/><br/>I struggled reading this book because it was very interesting at times but then it became very dull.   <span id="freeText9974919219543928224" style="display:none">This wasn't a very easy read. <br /><br />I'll start by saying that I started reading this book after I saw a Facebook comment claiming this is good literature. I was intrigued as Middle East history and people overcoming struggles are things I enjoy reading about. <br /><br />I struggled reading this book because it was very interesting at times but then it became very dull. So I found myself pushing through the dull parts, hoping that it would become interesting again. <br /><br />I feel like the observations about humans and cruelty were enlightening. There was something intelligent about this book, you can see they're journalists. <br /><br />This book lacked backstory. I found myself googling Irish history (cause yeah, can't be expected to know that) and I'm still not sure I understand why they were taken and why they were released. This could have been addressed more clearly. <br /><br />All in all, I'm happy I read this book, even if it was difficult. <br /><br /><b> what I'm taking with me </b> <br />• Humans can overcome with defiance and kindness. <br />• I can't share the sympathy Brian seems to feel for his captors. <br />• John sounds like an amazing person. </span>

<div id="review_788098882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/788098882" />
    <a title="Nicola Waldron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12614372-nicola-waldron"><img alt="Nicola Waldron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347023909p2/12614372.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/788098882?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola Waldron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola Waldron" href="/user/show/12614372-nicola-waldron">Nicola Waldron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer788098882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12340200499899185915">I've owned this book for 20 years or more now and finally felt ready to open it and read. Just remarkable -- a work to remind us how expansive is the human mind, proving that cultural (and religious) education is directly connected to the development of the heart, in the sense that, early on in life, we have the opportunity to either help open that heart through compassion and universal inclusion, or slam it shut by demanding blind obedience to dogma, along with all the heart-mind's potential fo</span>
  <span id="freeText12340200499899185915" style="display:none">I've owned this book for 20 years or more now and finally felt ready to open it and read. Just remarkable -- a work to remind us how expansive is the human mind, proving that cultural (and religious) education is directly connected to the development of the heart, in the sense that, early on in life, we have the opportunity to either help open that heart through compassion and universal inclusion, or slam it shut by demanding blind obedience to dogma, along with all the heart-mind's potential for good and beauty. A real life tragicomedy. And just exquisitely composed, in every sense of that word -- a soaring, utterly compelling symphony created from Keenan's cries of pain and philosophical musings, mixed with the laughter of his resilience, the tender banter exchanged with his fellow captive, John McCarthy, and the music that is silence. It's as if when you read, a light shines out, and you, in your turn, by reading, shine a light back into the soul of the writer, hence into the world -- reading as an act of solidarity and hope. Essential reading, truly, and not in any sense outdated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12340200499899185915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146365802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146365802" />
    <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth"><img alt="Kate Forsyth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329268435p2/3237560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146365802?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Forsyth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Forsyth" href="/user/show/3237560-kate-forsyth">Kate Forsyth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146365802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3826219533296914616">Brian Keenan is an Irish teacher who was kidnapped in 1985 while working in Beirut. This is a memoir of his four and a half years as a hostage, enduring torture, beatings, and solitary confinement. A very hard book to read at times – how can humans be so cruel? Yet Brian survived mind and soul intact, an amazing testament to the strength of his spirit. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_200083757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200083757" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5958401-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546517338p2/5958401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200083757?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/5958401-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText"> believers, lovers and philosphers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Peter by: </span>
      Claire Mallon
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=history-british">history-british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=anglo-irish">anglo-irish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=top-100">top-100</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=to-reread">to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=spiritual">spiritual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958401-peter?shelf=creme-de-la-creme">creme-de-la-creme</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200083757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer558126702308020412"><br/>This is the kind of book that leaves you ruminating. Like a good meal or sermon, you want to glean every last nuance and morsel from it ensuring that nothing is lost, that it all sinks in. A little like Primo Levi's 'If this is a Man' this book leaves you with a sense of awe, reverence even, for this 'beauty of the world, this paragon of animals', for what we are and what we are capable of. It reveals a depth of spirit, a nobility of character and the sheer belligerent will that enables one to f</span>
  <span id="freeText558126702308020412" style="display:none"><br />This is the kind of book that leaves you ruminating. Like a good meal or sermon, you want to glean every last nuance and morsel from it ensuring that nothing is lost, that it all sinks in. A little like Primo Levi's 'If this is a Man' this book leaves you with a sense of awe, reverence even, for this 'beauty of the world, this paragon of animals', for what we are and what we are capable of. It reveals a depth of spirit, a nobility of character and the sheer belligerent will that enables one to fight in the face of inhumane behaviour as well as a sadness at how far short we often fall.<br /><br />Brian Keenan is not just a good writer; his prose is poetic, descriptive and eloquent, but he is also a good thinker. A true philosopher with the capacity to honestly and unflinchingly look fallen man, the human shadow, in the face, within and without, in all it's ignorance, fear and brutality and over come it with faith, truth, dignity, humour and reason and in doing so, again akin to Primo Levi, he discovers himself; he is humanised, ennobled and empowered through the process.<br />Few people have been where these men have been, but everybody can take something away from their experience and find enrichment or hope especially when it is shared as honestly and eloquently s this. This book then is like a map on the life of the soul, marking the primal, wild, less travelled territory, frightening extremes of humanity's collective madness, need of redemption, and maybe even charting a way through it into compassion, brotherhood and community.<br /><br />The following quote is taken from John McCarthy's published account of the same events, McCarthy being Brian's cell mate in captivity;<br /><br />"Brian made me work my mind as I had never done before. He wants to understand everything, he always needs to know where he stands, where he's going and how best to get there....He has a great ability to explain abstract philosophical or political ideas through personal anecdotes. His language is brilliantly coloured with imagery and humour.....Talking with Brian took me on mental voyages that happily compensated for those physical journeys we were denied by circumstance. One of us would tell a tale, the other would respond and take the trip further, the ideas spread out, forming a progression, often drawing a circle and coming back, through stages of anger, laughter and sadness, to the point of departure. Yet we returned refreshed. We couldn't actually move, we were cramped, but we could grow."<br /><br />No wonder they became such close friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="558126702308020412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

How can you not just respect the honesty and courage to write about the mental and physical torment which assailed each of the captives Brian Keenan was held with during that time and especially his own.   <span id="freeText17773889679296167828" style="display:none">It is difficult to separate the ratings for the book as a book from the ratings of the story: of the immense suffering of a man held captive for four and a half years in appalling and brutal conditions. I am so glad I have read the book and have just a chink of understanding of what he and others went through. But as a book, it is not the best written of books. At times I felt frustrated by the fact that it is a telling. So...four stars. Should everyone read it? Yes.</span>

<div id="review_21204357" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21204357" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/975599-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21204357?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" rel="nofollow" href="/user/show/975599-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21204357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16497810075589611899">One of the most moving and perspective shifting books I have ever read. Keenan's story of captivity and exposure to a very broken segment of human society is highly topical in this day and age. Anyone who would seek to defend imprisonment without trial should read and consider this man's experiences.<br/><br/>While the second half of the book, his time in captivity with another hostage, does not quite live up to the intensity of the first hundred pages or so, it is still well worth reading. The first sect</span>
  <span id="freeText16497810075589611899" style="display:none">One of the most moving and perspective shifting books I have ever read. Keenan's story of captivity and exposure to a very broken segment of human society is highly topical in this day and age. Anyone who would seek to defend imprisonment without trial should read and consider this man's experiences.<br /><br />While the second half of the book, his time in captivity with another hostage, does not quite live up to the intensity of the first hundred pages or so, it is still well worth reading. The first section, on his time in solitude, has some absolutely amazing passages, that evoked a stronger emotional response in me than anything else I have ever read.<br /><br />Highly highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16497810075589611899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2032160124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2032160124" />
    <a title="Warren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64901540-warren"><img alt="Warren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2032160124?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warren" href="/user/show/64901540-warren">Warren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64901540-warren?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64901540-warren?shelf=biography">biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2032160124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12674056938587972197">This book is a testament to humanity, though not the idealised view of humanity in which we "ride above adversity because in the end the human spirit wins out." This is much too simplistic a view of humanity, and Keenan is much too clever a writer to adopt it. Yes, Keenan manages to face his brutal captivity with heroic fortitude; however, he is also sharply aware and critical of his own faults, which at times are easily forgiven and entertaining, but at others affect his friend and cellmate, Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText12674056938587972197" style="display:none">This book is a testament to humanity, though not the idealised view of humanity in which we "ride above adversity because in the end the human spirit wins out." This is much too simplistic a view of humanity, and Keenan is much too clever a writer to adopt it. Yes, Keenan manages to face his brutal captivity with heroic fortitude; however, he is also sharply aware and critical of his own faults, which at times are easily forgiven and entertaining, but at others affect his friend and cellmate, John McCarthy and are therefore less endearing. <br /><br />Moreover, what I found most fascinating about the book was Keenan's portrayal of the guards. They were just as human as he was ("...anything one human perpetrates against another cannot by its own logic be called inhuman," he ruminates at one point). These were not two-dimensional villains, but humans with desperate, misguided hopes and sinister, obsessive fears. One passage of the book was to me a powerful explanation of radicalization that could and should be used to understand the current threat of homegrown terrorism in Europe (as well as everywhere else). "They cannot find value in themselves. A man can then no longer surrender to such a monstrous condition of life. He seeks power, power that will restore his dignity and his manhood; that will let him stand with other men and know himelf to be their equal and restore him to the community of humanity." Keenan's recognition that his guards were in their own, psychological, prisons was what allowed him to overcome his ordeal. His raw honesty, at times funny, at others, difficult to read, makes this a book that the reader is unlikely to forget.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12674056938587972197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2762138538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2762138538" />
    <a title="Moore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10958164-moore"><img alt="Moore" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2762138538?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moore" href="/user/show/10958164-moore">Moore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10958164-moore?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2762138538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1716970636697035140">There’s something unseemly about the idea of ‘reviewing’ this book, this life, this unspeakable four years, this exploration of a vital relationship with John McCarthy- what comment can I offer? That it should have more action, more female characters, fewer Kalashnikovs? <br/><br/>It’s definitely a strange and unsettling read, and about half way through I found I had to look Brian Keenan up on YouTube- to hear his voice saying some of these things, to know that he survived, to feel his reflective tone- I </span>
  <span id="freeText1716970636697035140" style="display:none">There’s something unseemly about the idea of ‘reviewing’ this book, this life, this unspeakable four years, this exploration of a vital relationship with John McCarthy- what comment can I offer? That it should have more action, more female characters, fewer Kalashnikovs? <br /><br />It’s definitely a strange and unsettling read, and about half way through I found I had to look Brian Keenan up on YouTube- to hear his voice saying some of these things, to know that he survived, to feel his reflective tone- I couldn’t carry on on reading with my own voice. <br /><br />Listening to him it is extraordinary how much type he takes up with saying something about the men involved, friendship, kindness, seeking a way through, without really referring to God or religion that much. Also extraordinary how restrained he is about John’s personal information and things they must have thought or felt about each other. And perhaps that’s why it’s four rather than five stars for me. - there is a dimension missing, of fighting, or criticising one another or others that is missing. Rightly so perhaps, it would distract, detract from their exemplary survival/friendship mechanism. But it feels too like a parable without it - no thoughts of malice, sex, violence, bitching. I don’t think the book or their relationship could wear that - but without it, there’s something missing. <br /><br />Invariably, people talk about human spirit in assessing this book - I’d like to think that, that it is within any of us such survival, humour, kindness - but strongly suspect it’s HIM, or THEM- that love, fortitude, chemistry- it was them. It would not have been anybody else’s story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1716970636697035140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2292748030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2292748030" />
    <a title="Tammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25045472-tammy"><img alt="Tammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386903026p2/25045472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2292748030?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/25045472-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25045472-tammy?shelf=get-rid-off-stack">get-rid-off-stack</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292748030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13623168036177098221">It is difficult to rate this book. I feel like an absolute jerk giving it 2 stars, but as a piece of literature it just does not read well. The writer survived a harrowing experience and writing this book must have been therapeutic. There are some interesting details and a good observations about the guards carrying out the imprisonment. I do feel that Keenan would have greatly benefited from a stronger editor to better convey the experience and the impact as well as reduce the amount of 'tellin</span>
  <span id="freeText13623168036177098221" style="display:none">It is difficult to rate this book. I feel like an absolute jerk giving it 2 stars, but as a piece of literature it just does not read well. The writer survived a harrowing experience and writing this book must have been therapeutic. There are some interesting details and a good observations about the guards carrying out the imprisonment. I do feel that Keenan would have greatly benefited from a stronger editor to better convey the experience and the impact as well as reduce the amount of 'telling' and unnecessary babbling at points. In my opinion, the book ends irritatingly. There is no afterword, nothing to tell us about what happened to the other prisoners, what it was like to finally go back home, the readjustment, etc. That could all well have been for another book, but to leave me hanging about John? Annoying. I plan to read John McCarthy's book about the experience next. Hopefully it will be more rewarding.<br /><br />It takes a lot of courage to write a book like this, but it also takes a very good editor to have the courage to rein the writer in. As is, it is a somewhat rewarding read that unfortunately does not live up to its potential.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13623168036177098221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2360856260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360856260" />
    <a title="Ben Ballin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15815809-ben-ballin"><img alt="Ben Ballin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399829601p2/15815809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360856260?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Ballin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Ballin" href="/user/show/15815809-ben-ballin">Ben Ballin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360856260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9629830069232187080">The great thing about this book is how utterly honest an account it attempts to be. Keenan takes us on a mental and emotional journey through his horrific kidnapping and how he managed to survive it with his sense of self intact. Part of this was the extraordinary and mutually supportive bond that he formed with John McCarthy and other prisoners. Self-reflective in the extreme, he never loses sight of the way that this inhuman situation imprisons his captors too. It's a highly individualistic ac</span>
  <span id="freeText9629830069232187080" style="display:none">The great thing about this book is how utterly honest an account it attempts to be. Keenan takes us on a mental and emotional journey through his horrific kidnapping and how he managed to survive it with his sense of self intact. Part of this was the extraordinary and mutually supportive bond that he formed with John McCarthy and other prisoners. Self-reflective in the extreme, he never loses sight of the way that this inhuman situation imprisons his captors too. It's a highly individualistic accounts, warts and all, and doesn't shirk Keenan's own more difficult personality traits. By the end of if, I felt I knew him well and admired him greatly ... though was not wholly in tune with everything he had written. While I'd take issue with his generalisations about, for example, 'the Arab mind', I imagine that these too arose from the particularities of the grim and extreme experience he found himself in. A remarkable book.<br /> "Humanisation is a reciprocal thing. We cannot know ourselves or declare ourselves human unless we share in the humanity of another."</span>
  <a data-text-id="9629830069232187080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3063999991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3063999991" />
    <a title="Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5733902-sally"><img alt="Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591019856p2/5733902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3063999991?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sally" href="/user/show/5733902-sally">Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5733902-sally?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3063999991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17177661530693273917">I've read a few prison memoirs, and while you may feel immense sympathy, and while the writing process may have been cathartic, they tend to be pretty samey and dull.<br/>So I wasn't expecting to find this a *5 work, but it totally is. Brian Keenan had been away from Belfast on a teaching post, in Beirut for 4 months when he was kidnapped by islamic 'jihadists' and held prisoner for four and a half years. <br/>This is an entirely engrossing read as Keenan delves into the recesses of his mind to explain ho</span>
  <span id="freeText17177661530693273917" style="display:none">I've read a few prison memoirs, and while you may feel immense sympathy, and while the writing process may have been cathartic, they tend to be pretty samey and dull.<br />So I wasn't expecting to find this a *5 work, but it totally is. Brian Keenan had been away from Belfast on a teaching post, in Beirut for 4 months when he was kidnapped by islamic 'jihadists' and held prisoner for four and a half years. <br />This is an entirely engrossing read as Keenan delves into the recesses of his mind to explain how humans cope (or not) with the endless days of solitary confinement, the alternating friendly overtures and casual brutality of their jailers, the uncertainty - release now? later? or slaughter? ...and the mind numbing boredom. Eventually sharing a cell with fellow hostage John McCarthy (and at times with some Americans) he elaborates on the process of friendship amid such dire conditions. Their efforts to find amusement in makeshift games and humour, to confront their aggressors with whatever resistance they could.<br />Very memorable and well written account.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17177661530693273917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3465238233?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ed" href="/user/show/63222399-ed">Ed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780091752088" href="/book/show/1558618.An_Evil_Cradling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63222399-ed?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3465238233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15598793105232043378">This is probably the best book I've read in a month or two and I hope it sticks in my mind and I continue to think about what is said in it during the next few weeks.<br/><br/>Brian Keenan's abduction is presented with a beautiful mix of deep reflection on the meaning of the experience as well as the detailed minutiae of his environment, company and his captors. There is a remarkable weight to what he has to say, which stems as much from his unique experience as it does his own writing style. To have come</span>
  <span id="freeText15598793105232043378" style="display:none">This is probably the best book I've read in a month or two and I hope it sticks in my mind and I continue to think about what is said in it during the next few weeks.<br /><br />Brian Keenan's abduction is presented with a beautiful mix of deep reflection on the meaning of the experience as well as the detailed minutiae of his environment, company and his captors. There is a remarkable weight to what he has to say, which stems as much from his unique experience as it does his own writing style. To have come away from years of imprisonment, torture and abuse and be able to put down and share a narrative like this - which tells a detailed story containing good and evil, and very deep friendship - it is a wonderful thing.<br /><br />This should not be read by the young, but I think it should be on sixth form or university reading lists for the exploration of humanity, psychology and survival which it contains.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15598793105232043378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2850010691" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5032988061796245705">This is a truly haunting book, so much so that it hit me today, I cannot even remember what I was thinking about or why but suddenly it was there, from over 25 years ago, I remembered that I had read this book. I couldn't remember it's name (can't believe it now I've seen it!) but I remembered how it made me feel..<br/><br/>I was 10 at the time (someone put it in our little classroom library, in Ireland.. ) but even without having re-read it as an adult I remember thinking it was written well and it immer</span>
  <span id="freeText5032988061796245705" style="display:none">This is a truly haunting book, so much so that it hit me today, I cannot even remember what I was thinking about or why but suddenly it was there, from over 25 years ago, I remembered that I had read this book. I couldn't remember it's name (can't believe it now I've seen it!) but I remembered how it made me feel..<br /><br />I was 10 at the time (someone put it in our little classroom library, in Ireland.. ) but even without having re-read it as an adult I remember thinking it was written well and it immersed you in, what was, a horrific, heartbreaking and truly brutal true story.<br /><br />Not for the faint-hearted but definitely one for those who go in search of the "well written truth".<br /><br />This book will make you cry one minute and then make you laugh the next, I am remembering that now too, from 25 years ago. This book will make an impact.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3229279709?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/830760-sue?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/830760-sue?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3229279709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14454706776294810410">A sometimes harrowing but never gratuitous account of the author's experiences as a hostage in Lebanon in the late 1980s. Superb writing, full of compassion and honesty, tinged with some violence and extreme emotion. I had not expected to enjoy this book, nor to find it so very readable, but it was a selection for my local reading group, and turned out to be an excellent choice. <br/><br/>There's some dark humour here and there, and a light touch as the author writes as if observing his reactions at times</span>
  <span id="freeText14454706776294810410" style="display:none">A sometimes harrowing but never gratuitous account of the author's experiences as a hostage in Lebanon in the late 1980s. Superb writing, full of compassion and honesty, tinged with some violence and extreme emotion. I had not expected to enjoy this book, nor to find it so very readable, but it was a selection for my local reading group, and turned out to be an excellent choice. <br /><br />There's some dark humour here and there, and a light touch as the author writes as if observing his reactions at times. I don't know when I last found a non-fiction book as compulsive as this one - I expected to skim, but (other than a few poems) read every word.<br /><br />Very highly recommended. <br /><br />Longer review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://suesbookreviews.blogspot.com/2020/06/an-evil-cradling-by-brian-keenan.html">https://suesbookreviews.blogspot.com/...</a></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uk6SE1oPkygamYucxWiGkQrGcJh7ajjTEdTiJBvue6+NjXu6f08+l/8B6a80tjtFl4XbCxSwgxgujeAfligQtw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mEd9iVBQnJKcO1BuAaSYkO4LK5FD5I05aLJ31oz+dDSvhJQgdRAxLXmjMl3weiVEc0iAAiw+NvJX63XtATgfLA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1551122-an-evil-cradling">Quotes from An Evil Cradling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Cruelty and fear are man-made, and men who perpetrate them are ruled by them. Such men are only half-made things. They live out their unresolved lives by attempting to destroy anything that challenges the void in themselves. A child holds a blanket over its face in fear. A fear-filled man transposes his inadequacy onto another. He blames them, hates them, and hopes to rid himself of his unloved self by hurting, or worse, destroying them.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9140652-cruelty-and-fear-are-man-made-and-men-who-perpetrate-them">4 likes</a>

          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
